We determined the approximate value for <i>V</i>. <i>vinifera</i> (<i>λ</i><sub>Vv</sub>) using the above estimator, and used it to assess the correction coefficient ratio for each species. The major-eudicot common hexaploidy 115–130 Ma (refs. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Vekemans, D. et al. Gamma paleohexaploidy in the stem lineage of core eudicots: significance for MADS-box gene and species diversification. Mol. Biol. Evol. 29, 3793–3806 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2403">55</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Jiao, Y. N. et al. Ancestral polyploidy in seed plants and angiosperms. Nature 473, 97–100 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2406">56</a></sup>), inferred by grape duplicated genes, was used as the reference to date the ages for the other polyploidization and speciation events (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">12</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Phylogenetic analyses</h3><p>To infer the phylogenetic placements of <i>E. ferox</i> and <i>C. demersum</i>, SSCGs were first identified using SonicParanoid<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Cosentino, S. &amp; Iwasaki, W. SonicParanoid: fast, accurate and easy orthology inference. Bioinformatics 35, 149–151 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2427">32</a></sup> v.1.0 from 14 seed plants (SSCG; Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">13</a>). For each gene, amino acid sequences were aligned using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Katoh, K., Misawa, K., Kuma, K. &amp; Miyata, T. MAFFT: a novel method for rapid multiple sequence alignment based on fast Fourier transform. Nucleic Acids Res. 30, 3059–3066 (2002)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2434">57</a></sup> v.7.402, and then DNA sequences were aligned according to the corresponding amino acid alignments using PAL2NAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Suyama, M., Torrents, D. &amp; Bork, P. PAL2NAL: robust conversion of protein sequence alignments into the corresponding codon alignments. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, W609–W612 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2439">58</a></sup> v.14. For datasets SSCG-CDS and SSCG-Codon12, the maximum likelihood (ML) trees were inferred from concatenated gene sequences using IQ-TREE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Nguyen, L. T., Schmidt, H. A., von Haeseler, A. &amp; Minh, B. Q. IQ-TREE: a fast and effective stochastic algorithm for estimating maximum-likelihood phylogenies. Mol. Biol. Evol. 32, 268–274 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2443">59</a></sup> v.1.6.9, which automatically selected the best-fit substitution model using ModelFinder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Kalyaanamoorthy, S., Minh, B. Q., Wong, T. K. F., von Haeseler, A. &amp; Jermiin, L. S. ModelFinder: fast model selection for accurate phylogenetic estimates. Nat. Methods 14, 587–589 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2447">60</a></sup>. Bootstrap support was estimated using 1,000 replicates of the ultrafast bootstrap approximation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Hoang, D. T., Chernomor, O., von Haeseler, A., Minh, B. Q. &amp; Vinh, L. S. UFBoot2: improving the ultrafast bootstrap approximation. Mol. Biol. Evol. 35, 518–522 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2451">61</a></sup> (-bb 1000 -m MFP). For coalescent-based analyses, gene trees were first estimated using IQ-TREE; the gene trees were then utilized by ASTRAL v.5.6.1 to infer species trees with quartet scores and posterior probabilities. Furthermore, SSCGs were identified using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. Jr &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2455">36</a></sup> v.2.0.9 (OSCG) with one more Gymnosperm (<i>P. abies</i>; Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">13</a>). Species trees were inferred from the datasets OSCG-CDS and OSCG-Codon12 using concatenation and coalescent methods as described above. Finally, we extracted low-copy genes from 15 seed plants (LCG). Here, each gene was required to include at least 1 sequence from each of the 15 species and less than 5 homologous sequences per species. For the datasets LCG-CDS and LCG-Codon12, gene trees were first estimated using IQ-TREE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Nguyen, L. T., Schmidt, H. A., von Haeseler, A. &amp; Minh, B. Q. IQ-TREE: a fast and effective stochastic algorithm for estimating maximum-likelihood phylogenies. Mol. Biol. Evol. 32, 268–274 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2466">59</a></sup>; these gene trees were then utilized to construct species trees using STAG<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Emms, D. &amp; Kelly, S. STAG: species tree inference from all genes. Preprint at &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1101/267914&#xA;&#xA; (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2470">37</a></sup> v.1.0.0.</p><p>For plastid genes, the 72 CDS of protein-coding genes were extracted from 15 seed plants (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">14</a>), and aligned using MAFFT and PAL2NAL as described above. The ML trees were inferred from concatenated gene sequences using RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312–1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2480">62</a></sup> v.7.2.8 with 100 bootstraps.</p><p>For expanded taxon sampling, sequence similarity was first assessed for all of the amino acid sequences from 213 species (211 angiosperms and 2 gymnosperms; Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">15</a>) using MMseqs2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Steinegger, M. &amp; Soding, J. MMseqs2 enables sensitive protein sequence searching for the analysis of massive data sets. Nat. Biotechnol. 35, 1026–1028 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2490">63</a></sup> with an <i>E-</i>value threshold of 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>, and then grouped using a Markov cluster algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Enright, A. J., Van Dongen, S. &amp; Ouzounis, C. A. An efficient algorithm for large-scale detection of protein families. Nucleic Acids Res. 30, 1575–1584 (2002)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2499">64</a></sup>. Here, each gene was required to include sequences from more than 180 species. Next, ‘mostly’ single-copy orthologous genes (SCOG) were identified using a tree‐based method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Yang, Y. &amp; Smith, S. A. Orthology inference in nonmodel organisms using transcriptomes and low-coverage genomes: improving accuracy and matrix occupancy for phylogenomics. Mol. Biol. Evol. 31, 3081–3092 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2504">65</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="De Smet, R. et al. Convergent gene loss following gene and genome duplications creates single-copy families in flowering plants. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 110, 2898–2903 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2507">66</a></sup>. Each gene was aligned using MAFFT and PAL2NAL as described above, and species trees were inferred from datasets SCOG-CDS and SCOG-Codon12 using ASTRAL.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Visualizations of gene-tree discordance</h3><p>Gene trees were first converted to ultrametric trees using the R package Phybase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Liu, L. &amp; Yu, L. Phybase: an R package for species tree analysis. Bioinformatics 26, 962–963 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2519">67</a></sup>, and then superimposed using DensiTree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Bouckaert, R. R. DensiTree: making sense of sets of phylogenetic trees. Bioinformatics 26, 1372–1373 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2523">38</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#Fig2">2c</a>). Quartet frequencies of the internal branches in the species tree were calculated using ASTRAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Zhang, C., Rabiee, M., Sayyari, E. &amp; Mirarab, S. ASTRAL-III: polynomial time species tree reconstruction from partially resolved gene trees. BMC Bioinform. 19, 153 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2530">33</a></sup> with the parameter ‘-t=2’ (Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">17</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">19</a>). Furthermore, the analysis of gene-tree compatibility was conducted using DiscoVista<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Sayyari, E., Whitfield, J. B. &amp; Mirarab, S. DiscoVista: interpretable visualizations of gene tree discordance. Mol. Phylogenet. Evol. 122, 110–115 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2541">39</a></sup> v.1.0. Here, a total of 15 species groups were considered, and 7 of which are identified in our species tree, including: (1) 12 Mesagiospermae, (2) 4 eudicots, (3) 3 magnollids, (4) 3 monocots, (5) <i>Euryale</i> and all Mesangiospermaes, (6) Ceratophyllaceae and eudicots, and (7) Magnoliids and (Ceratophyllaceae and eudicots). The other 8 species groups were: (1) basal angiosperms (that is, <i>Ambrorella</i> and <i>Euryale</i>), (2) <i>Ambrorella</i> and Mesangiospermae, (3) Ceratophyllaceae and magnoliids, (4) Ceratophyllaceae and monocots, (5) magnoliids and eudicots, (6) magnoliids and monocots, (7) eudicots and monocots, and (8) Ceratophyllaceae, magnoliids and monocots (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#Fig2">2e</a>, Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">18</a>). Bootstrap support values of at least 75% were interpreted as highly supported<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Jarvis, E. D. et al. Whole-genome analyses resolve early branches in the tree of life of modern birds. Science 346, 1320–1331 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2564">68</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#Fig2">2e</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Divergence time estimation</h3><p>Divergence time was estimated for the dataset SSCG-CDS using the program MCMCTree in the PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2579">53</a></sup> package v.4.9 h. After a burn-in of 5,000,000 iterations, the MCMC process was performed 20,000 times with sample frequency of 5,000. Convergence was assessed using two independent runs. We used the following age constraints in our estimation procedure: the divergence between angiosperms and gymnosperms (330–289 Ma; <a href="http://www.timetree.org/">http://www.timetree.org/</a>), the crown group of angiosperms (267–132.9 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Li, H. T. et al. Origin of angiosperms and the puzzle of the Jurassic gap. Nat. Plants 5, 461–470 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2587">4</a></sup>, the crown group of monocots (184–113 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Li, H. T. et al. Origin of angiosperms and the puzzle of the Jurassic gap. Nat. Plants 5, 461–470 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2591">4</a></sup> and the crown group of eudicots (161–125 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Li, H. T. et al. Origin of angiosperms and the puzzle of the Jurassic gap. Nat. Plants 5, 461–470 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2595">4</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Hybridization inference and ILS simulation</h3><p>Hybridization was detected for the dataset OSCG-CDS using the maximum pseudolikelihood estimation of phylogenetic networks, as implemented in PhyloNetworks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Solis-Lemus, C., Bastide, P. &amp; Ane, C. PhyloNetworks: a package for phylogenetic networks. Mol. Biol. Evol. 34, 3292–3298 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2608">69</a></sup> v.0.9.0. The maximum allowed number of hybridizations was set from hmax=0 to hmax=10, each with 100 runs. The ILS simulation was performed as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang, K. et al. Incomplete lineage sorting rather than hybridization explains the inconsistent phylogeny of the wisent. Commun. Biol. 1, 169 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2612">70</a></sup>. We simulated 200,000 gene trees under the multispecies coalescent model using the R function sim.coaltree.sp as implemented in the package Phybase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Liu, L. &amp; Yu, L. Phybase: an R package for species tree analysis. Bioinformatics 26, 962–963 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2616">67</a></sup> v.1.5. The internal branch lengths of the ASTRAL tree were used for the simulation, and all terminal branches were set to 1 (as 1 allele was generated for each species). It should be noted that internal branch lengths (in coalescent units) in our simulation might have been overestimated, as the cause of gene tree heterogeneity was assumed to result from only ILS. Gene-tree quartet frequencies were calculated for simulated and empirical datasets, and the correlation test was performed using the cor.test function in R.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Demographic inference</h3><p>The pairwise sequentially Markovian coalescent (PSMC) model<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Inference of human population history from individual whole-genome sequences. Nature 475, 493–496 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2628">71</a></sup> v.0.6.4-r49 was used to infer the demographic history of seven species, that is, <i>A</i>. <i>trichopoda</i> (Amborellales), <i>E. ferox</i> (Nymphaeales), <i>C. demersum</i> (Ceratophyllales), <i>C. kanehirae</i> (magnoliids), <i>L</i>. <i>chinense</i> (magnoliids), <i>P</i>. <i>equestris</i> (monocots) and <i>V</i>. <i>vinifera</i> (eudicots). The genome of <i>E</i>. <i>ferox</i> showed very low heterozygosity (about 0.02%; Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">22</a>) and, therefore, two individuals were included in the PSMC analysis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Thomas, C. G. et al. Full-genome evolutionary histories of selfing, splitting, and selection in Caenorhabditis. Genome Res. 25, 667–678 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2676">72</a></sup>. For each species, whole-genome resequencing data (at least 30-fold coverage) were obtained from NCBI (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM1">22</a>). Reads were mapped to the assembled genome, and the consensus sequences were extracted. The analysis was performed using the following parameters: -N25 -t15 -r5 -p ‘4+25×2+4+6’. Here, for <i>A. trichopoda</i>, <i>C kanehirae</i>, <i>L. chinense</i> and <i>V</i>. <i>vinifera</i>, the generation time and mutation rate were obtained from previous studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Amborella Genome Project. The Amborella genome and the evolution of flowering plants. Science 342, 1241089 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2699">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Chaw, S.-M. et al. Stout camphor tree genome fills gaps in understanding of flowering plant genome evolution. Nat. Plants 5, 63–73 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2702">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Chen, J. et al. Liriodendron genome sheds light on angiosperm phylogeny and species–pair differentiation. Nat. Plants 5, 18–25 (2019)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2705">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Zhou, Y., Massonnet, M., Sanjak, J. S., Cantu, D. &amp; Gaut, B. S. Evolutionary genomics of grape (Vitis vinifera ssp. vinifera) domestication. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 114, 11715–11720 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2708">73</a></sup>. For other three species (that is, <i>E. ferox</i>, <i>C. demersum</i> and <i>P</i>. <i>equestris</i>), the mutation rate was first estimated using r8s<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Sanderson, M. J. r8s: inferring absolute rates of molecular evolution and divergence times in the absence of a molecular clock. Bioinformatics 19, 301–302 (2003)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2725">74</a></sup>. Furthermore, as <i>E. ferox</i> is an annual species, the generation time was set to 1. For perennial species, as the generation time is difficult to determine precisely<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Petit, R. J. &amp; Hampe, A. Some evolutionary consequences of being a tree. Annu. Rev. Ecol. Evol. Syst. 37, 187–214 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d12344e2733">75</a></sup>, we tested the generation time for both 3 and 5 years, and similar results were obtained.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-020-0594-6#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>All of the raw sequence reads used in this study have been deposited at NCBI under the BioProject accession numbers <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA552436">PRJNA552436</a> (<i>E. ferox</i>) and <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA552433">PRJNA552433</a> (<i>C. demersum</i>). The assemblies and annotations are available from the CoGe comparative genomics platform at <a href="https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56574">https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56574</a> (<i>E. ferox</i> chromosome assembly), <a href="https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56571">https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56571</a> (<i>E. ferox</i> contig assembly), <a href="https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56572">https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56572</a> (<i>C. demersum</i> chromosome assembly) and <a href="https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56569">https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=56569</a> (<i>C. demersum</i> contig assembly).</p>
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="code-availability" data-title="Code availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="code-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="code-availability">Code availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="code-availability-content">
              
              <p>The custom scripts have deposited in GitHub (<a href="https://github.com/yongzhiyang2012/Euryale_ferox_and_Ceratophyllum_demersum_genome_analysis">https://github.com/yongzhiyang2012/Euryale_ferox_and_Ceratophyllum_demersum_genome_analysis</a>).</p>

                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="headline" content="Drinnan, A. N., Crane, P. R. &amp; Hoot, S. Y.Y., L.L., D.W. and D.R. performed the assembly of the two genomes. Y.Y., L.L., T.M. and D.R. carried out the repeat and gene annotations.             </li>

      </div>

    </section>
